         </span>
         77
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bill Clinton presented Kurzweil with the National Medal of Technology during a White House ceremony in recognition of Kurzweil's development of computer-based technologies to help the disabled.
      </li>
      <li>
       The 2000 Telluride Tech Festival Award of Technology.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         78
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two other individuals also received the same honor that year. The award is presented yearly to people who "exemplify the life, times and standard of contribution of Tesla, Westinghouse and Nunn."
      </li>
      <li>
       The 2001
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lemelson-MIT_Prize" title="Lemelson-MIT Prize">
        Lemelson-MIT Prize
       </a>
       for a lifetime of developing technologies to help the disabled and to enrich the arts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         79
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Only one is awarded each year - it is given to highly successful, mid-career inventors. A $500,000 award accompanies the prize.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         80
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Kurzweil was inducted into the National Inventors Hall of Fame in 2002 for inventing the Kurzweil Reading Machine.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         81
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The organization "honors the women and men responsible for the great technological advances that make human, social and economic progress possible."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         82
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Fifteen other people were inducted into the Hall of Fame the same year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         83
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke" title="Arthur C. Clarke">
        Arthur C. Clarke
       </a>
       Lifetime Achievement Award on April 20, 2009 for lifetime achievement as an inventor and futurist in computer-based technologies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         84
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2011, Kurzweil was named a Senior Fellow of the
       <a href="/wiki/Design_Futures_Council" title="Design Futures Council">
        Design Futures Council
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         85
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2013, Kurzweil was honored as a Silicon Valley Visionary Award winner on June 26 by SVForum
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         86
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       In 2014, Kurzweil was honored with the American Visionary Art Museums Grand Visionary Award on January 30.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         87
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         88
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         89
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Kurzweil has received 20 honorary doctorates in science, engineering, music and humane letters from Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute, Hofstra University and other leading colleges and universities, as well as honors from three U.S. presidents - Clinton, Reagan and Johnson.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KurzweilAIbio_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-KurzweilAIbio-5">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         5
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         90
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Kurzweil has received seven national and international film awards including the CINE Golden Eagle Award and the Gold Medal for Science Education from the International Film and TV Festival of New York.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kurzweilai.net_72-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-kurzweilai.net-72">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         72
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">
       Criticism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ray_Kurzweil&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Criticism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This article's
         <i>
          Criticism
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          Controversy
         </i>
         section
         <b>
          may compromise the article's
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">
           neutral point of view
          </a>
          of the subject
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Article_structure" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">
           integrate the section's contents
          </a>
          into the article as a whole, or rewrite the material.
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (March 2013)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Kurzweil's ideas have generated criticism within the scientific community and in the media.
     </p>
     <p>
      Although the idea of a technological singularity is a popular concept in science fiction, some authors such as
      <a href="/wiki/Neal_Stephenson" title="Neal Stephenson">
       Neal Stephenson
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Sterling" title="Bruce Sterling">
       Bruce Sterling
      </a>
      have voiced skepticism about its real-world plausibility. Sterling expressed his views on the singularity scenario in a talk at the
      <a href="/wiki/Long_Now_Foundation" title="Long Now Foundation">
       Long Now Foundation
      </a>
      entitled
      <i>
       The Singularity: Your Future as a Black Hole
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other prominent AI thinkers and computer scientists such as
      <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Dennett" title="Daniel Dennett">
       Daniel Dennett
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Brooks" title="Rodney Brooks">
       Rodney Brooks
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Gelernter" title="David Gelernter">
       David Gelernter
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen" title="Paul Allen">
       Paul Allen
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      also criticized Kurzweil's projections.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lyons" title="Daniel Lyons">
       Daniel Lyons
      </a>
      , writing in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">
        Newsweek
       </a>
      </i>
      , criticized Kurzweil for some of his predictions that turned out to be wrong, such as the economy continuing to boom from the 1998
      <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">
       dot-com
      </a>
      through 2009, a US company having a
      <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">
       market capitalization
      </a>
      of more than $1 trillion, a supercomputer achieving 20
      <a href="/wiki/FLOPS" title="FLOPS">
       petaflops
      </a>
      , speech recognition being in widespread use and cars that would drive themselves using sensors installed in highways; all by 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To the charge that a 20 petaflop supercomputer was not produced in the time he predicted, Kurzweil responded that he considers
      <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
       Google
      </a>
      a giant supercomputer, and that it is indeed capable of 20 petaflops.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2_98-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the cover article of the December 2010 issue of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/IEEE_Spectrum" title="IEEE Spectrum">
        IEEE Spectrum
       </a>
      </i>
      , John Rennie criticizes Kurzweil for several predictions that failed to become manifest by the originally predicted date. "Therein lie the frustrations of Kurzweil's brand of tech punditry. On close examination, his clearest and most successful predictions often lack originality or profundity. And most of his predictions come with so many loopholes that they border on the unfalsifiable."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Joy" title="Bill Joy">
       Bill Joy
      </a>
      , cofounder of
      <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">
       Sun Microsystems
      </a>
      , agrees with Kurzweil's timeline of future progress, but thinks that technologies such as AI, nanotechnology and advanced biotechnology will create a
      <a href="/wiki/Dystopia" title="Dystopia">
       dystopian
      </a>
      world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Kapor" title="Mitch Kapor">
       Mitch Kapor
      </a>
      , the founder of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lotus_Development_Corporation" title="Lotus Development Corporation">
       Lotus Development Corporation
      </a>
      , has called the notion of a technological singularity "
      <a href="/wiki/Intelligent_design" title="Intelligent design">
       intelligent design
      </a>
      for the
      <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">
       IQ
      </a>
      140 people...This proposition that we're heading to this point at which everything is going to be just unimaginably differentit's fundamentally, in my view, driven by a religious impulse. And all of the frantic arm-waving can't obscure that fact for me."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some critics have argued more strongly against Kurzweil and his ideas. Cognitive scientist
      <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Hofstadter" title="Douglas Hofstadter">
       Douglas Hofstadter
      </a>
      has said of Kurzweil's and
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Moravec" title="Hans Moravec">
       Hans Moravec
      </a>
      's books: "It's an intimate mixture of rubbish and good ideas, and it's very hard to disentangle the two, because these are smart people; they're not stupid."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Biologist
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P.Z._Myers" title="P.Z. Myers">
       P. Z. Myers
      </a>
      has criticized Kurzweil's predictions as being based on "
      <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">
       New Age
      </a>
      spiritualism" rather than science and says that Kurzweil does not understand basic
      <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">
       biology
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singularitarianism_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Singularitarianism-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      VR pioneer
      <a href="/wiki/Jaron_Lanier" title="Jaron Lanier">
       Jaron Lanier
      </a>
      has even described Kurzweil's ideas as "cybernetic totalism" and has outlined his views on the culture surrounding Kurzweil's predictions in an essay for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edge.org" title="Edge.org">
       Edge.org
      </a>
      entitled
      <i>
       One Half of a Manifesto
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ieet_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ieet-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a critical review of Kurzweil's book
      <i>
       How to Create a Mind: The Secret of Human Thought Revealed
      </i>
      , philosopher
      <a href="/wiki/Colin_McGinn" title="Colin McGinn">
       Colin McGinn
      </a>
      refers to "the hype so blatantly brandished in its title" and asks: "He is clearly a man of many partsbut is ultimate theoretician of the mind one of them?" McGinn calls Kurzweil's claim that pattern recognition is the key to mental phenomena "obviously false" and concludes that the book is "interesting in places, fairly readable, moderately informative, but wildly overstated".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_N._Gray" title="John N. Gray">
       John Gray
      </a>
      , the British philosopher, argues that contemporary science is what magic was for ancient civilizations. It gives a sense of hope for those who are willing to do almost anything in order to achieve eternal life. He quotes Kurzweil's Singularity as another example of a trend which has almost always been present in the history of mankind.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Nassim_Nicholas_Taleb" title="Nassim Nicholas Taleb">
       Nassim Nicholas Taleb
      </a>
      , Lebanese American essayist, scholar and statistician, criticized his approach of taking multiple pills to achieve longevity in his book
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Antifragile" title="Antifragile">
        Antifragile
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>

       <li id="cite_note-4">

         </b>
         (3):737-93
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-KurzweilAIbio-5">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-KurzweilAIbio_5-0">
          <sup>
           <i>

       <li id="cite_note-90">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-90">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://people.forbes.com/profile/raymond-kurzweil/146841" rel="nofollow">
           "Raymond Kurzweil,"
          </a>
          .
          <i>

          <span class="reference-accessdate">

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=Raymond+Kurzweil%2C&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fpeople.forbes.com%2Fprofile%2Fraymond-kurzweil%2F146841&amp;rft.jtitle=Forbes&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-91">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-91">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Miller, Robin (2004-10-20).
          <a class="external text" href="http://interviews.slashdot.org/article.pl?sid=04/10/20/1518217" rel="nofollow">
           "Neal Stephenson Responds With Wit and Humor"
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Slashdot" title="Slashdot">
           Slashdot
          </a>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2008-08-28
           </span>
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           My thoughts are more in line with those of Jaron Lanier, who points out that while hardware might be getting faster all the time, software is shit (I am paraphrasing his argument). And without software to do something useful with all that hardware, the hardware's nothing more than a really complicated space heater.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.aufirst=Robin&amp;rft.aulast=Miller&amp;rft.au=Miller%2C+Robin&amp;rft.btitle=Neal+Stephenson+Responds+With+Wit+and+Humor&amp;rft.date=2004-10-20&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Finterviews.slashdot.org%2Farticle.pl%3Fsid%3D04%2F10%2F20%2F1518217&amp;rft.pub=Slashdot&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-92">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-92">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Brand, Stewart (2004-06-14).
          <a class="external text" href="http://blog.longnow.org/2004/06/14/bruce-sterling-the-singularity-your-future-as-a-black-hole/" rel="nofollow">
           "Bruce Sterling  "The Singularity: Your Future as a Black Hole
           <span style="padding-right:0.2em;">
            "
           </span>
           "
          </a>
          . The Long Now Foundation
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2009-06-08
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.au=Brand%2C+Stewart&amp;rft.aufirst=Stewart&amp;rft.aulast=Brand&amp;rft.btitle=Bruce+Sterling+%E2%80%93+%22The+Singularity%3A+Your+Future+as+a+Black+Hole%22&amp;rft.date=2004-06-14&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fblog.longnow.org%2F2004%2F06%2F14%2Fbruce-sterling-the-singularity-your-future-as-a-black-hole%2F&amp;rft.pub=The+Long+Now+Foundation&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-93">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-93">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Sterling" title="Bruce Sterling">
           Sterling, Bruce
          </a>
          .
          <a class="external text" href="http://media.longnow.org/seminars/salt-0200406-sterling/salt-0200406-sterling.mp3" rel="nofollow">
           "The Singularity: Your Future as a Black Hole"
          </a>
          <span style="font-size:85%;">
           (MP3)
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           It's an end-of-history notion, and like most end-of-history notions, it is showing its age.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.aufirst=Bruce&amp;rft.aulast=Sterling&amp;rft.au=Sterling%2C+Bruce&amp;rft.btitle=The+Singularity%3A+Your+Future+as+a+Black+Hole&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fmedia.longnow.org%2Fseminars%2Fsalt-0200406-sterling%2Fsalt-0200406-sterling.mp3&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-94">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-94">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Dennett" title="Daniel Dennett">
           Dennett, Daniel
          </a>
          .
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.edge.org/discourse/jaron_manifesto.html#dennett" rel="nofollow">
           "The Reality Club: One Half Of A Manifesto"
          </a>
          .
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edge.org" title="Edge.org">
           Edge.org
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           I'm glad that Lanier entertains the hunch that Dawkins and I (and Hofstadter and others) 'see some flaw in logic that insulates [our] thinking from the eschatalogical implications' drawn by Kurzweil and Moravec. He's right. I, for one, do see such a flaw, and I expect Dawkins and Hofstadter would say the same.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.au=Dennett%2C+Daniel&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel&amp;rft.aulast=Dennett&amp;rft.btitle=The+Reality+Club%3A+One+Half+Of+A+Manifesto&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.edge.org%2Fdiscourse%2Fjaron_manifesto.html%23dennett&amp;rft.pub=Edge.org&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-95">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-95">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Brooks" title="Rodney Brooks">
           Brooks, Rodney
          </a>
          .
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.edge.org/discourse/jaron_manifesto.html#brooks" rel="nofollow">
           "The Reality Club: One Half Of A Manifesto"
          </a>
          . Edge.org.
          <q>
           I do not at all agree with Moravec and Kurzweil's predictions for an eschatological cataclysm, just in time for their own memories and thoughts and person hood to be preserved before they might otherwise die.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.au=Brooks%2C+Rodney&amp;rft.aufirst=Rodney&amp;rft.aulast=Brooks&amp;rft.btitle=The+Reality+Club%3A+One+Half+Of+A+Manifesto&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.edge.org%2Fdiscourse%2Fjaron_manifesto.html%23brooks&amp;rft.pub=Edge.org&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-96">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-96">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Transcript of debate over feasibility of near-term AI (moderated by Rodney Brooks):
         <span class="citation web">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.edge.org/discourse/jaron_manifesto.html#brooks" rel="nofollow">
           "Gelernter, Kurzweil debate machine consciousness"
          </a>
          . KurzweilAI.net.
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.btitle=Gelernter%2C+Kurzweil+debate+machine+consciousness&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.edge.org%2Fdiscourse%2Fjaron_manifesto.html%23brooks&amp;rft.pub=KurzweilAI.net&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-97">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-97">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen" title="Paul Allen">
           Allen, Paul
          </a>
          .
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.technologyreview.com/view/425733/paul-allen-the-singularity-isnt-near/" rel="nofollow">
           "The Singularity Isn't Near"
          </a>
          .
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technology_Review" title="Technology Review">
           Technology Review
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           Kurzweil's reasoning rests on the Law of Accelerating Returns and its siblings, but these are not physical laws. They are assertions about how past rates of scientific and technical progress can predict the future rate. Therefore, like other attempts to forecast the future from the past, these "laws" will work until they don't.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.au=Allen%2C+Paul&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul&amp;rft.aulast=Allen&amp;rft.btitle=The+Singularity+Isn%27t+Near&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.technologyreview.com%2Fview%2F425733%2Fpaul-allen-the-singularity-isnt-near%2F&amp;rft.pub=Technology+Review&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2-98">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2_98-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Newsweek_May_2009_page_2_98-1">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             b
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Lyons, Daniel (May 2009).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.newsweek.com/id/197812/page/2" rel="nofollow">
           "I, Robot"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Newsweek
          </i>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2009-05-22
           </span>
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           During the height of the dotcom boom in 1998, Kurzweil predicted that the economy would keep on booming right through 2009 and that at least one U.S. company would have a market capitalization of more than $1 trillion, neither of which occurred. Kurzweil also predict-ed that by 2009 a top supercomputer would be capable of performing 20
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petaflop" title="Petaflop">
            petaflops
           </a>
           , the same as the human brain. In fact, the top supercomputer at the time, the
           <a href="/wiki/IBM_Roadrunner" title="IBM Roadrunner">
            IBM Roadrunner
           </a>
           , was capable of only 1.456 petaflops mark. Kurzweil also predicted that by now our cars would be able to drive themselves by communicating with intelligent sensors embedded in highways, and that speech recognition would be in widespread use.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=I%2C+Robot&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel&amp;rft.aulast=Lyons&amp;rft.au=Lyons%2C+Daniel&amp;rft.date=May+2009&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.newsweek.com%2Fid%2F197812%2Fpage%2F2&amp;rft.jtitle=Newsweek&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-99">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-99">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Rennie, John (December 2010).
          <a class="external text" href="http://spectrum.ieee.org/computing/software/ray-kurzweils-slippery-futurism/" rel="nofollow">
           "Ray Kurzweil's Slippery Futurism"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/IEEE_Spectrum" title="IEEE Spectrum">
            IEEE Spectrum
           </a>
          </i>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">

           <span class="nowrap">
            2012-08-13

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=Ray+Kurzweil%27s+Slippery+Futurism&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.aulast=Rennie&amp;rft.au=Rennie%2C+John&amp;rft.date=December+2010&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fspectrum.ieee.org%2Fcomputing%2Fsoftware%2Fray-kurzweils-slippery-futurism%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=IEEE+Spectrum&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-100">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-100">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation news">
          Joy, Bill (April 2000).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.wired.com/wired/archive/8.04/joy_pr.html" rel="nofollow">
           "Why the future doesn't need us"
          </a>

          <i>

          </i>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">

          <q>
           ...it was only in the autumn of 1998 that I became anxiously aware of how great are the dangers facing us in the 21st century. I can date the onset of my unease to the day I met Ray Kurzweil...
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=Why+the+future+doesn%27t+need+us&amp;rft.aufirst=Bill&amp;rft.au=Joy%2C+Bill&amp;rft.aulast=Joy&amp;rft.date=April+2000&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.wired.com%2Fwired%2Farchive%2F8.04%2Fjoy_pr.html&amp;rft.jtitle=Wired&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">

       <li id="cite_note-101">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=The+smartest+%28or+the+nuttiest%29+futurist+on+Earth&amp;rft.aufirst=Brian&amp;rft.aulast=O%27Keefe&amp;rft.au=O%27Keefe%2C+Brian&amp;rft.date=2007-05-02&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fmoney.cnn.com%2Fmagazines%2Ffortune%2Ffortune_archive%2F2007%2F05%2F14%2F100008848%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=Fortune&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">

        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-102">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-102">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Ross, Greg.
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.americanscientist.org/bookshelf/pub/douglas-r-hofstadter" rel="nofollow">
           "An interview with Douglas R. Hofstadter"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/American_Scientist" title="American Scientist">

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=An+interview+with+Douglas+R.+Hofstadter&amp;rft.aufirst=Greg&amp;rft.aulast=Ross&amp;rft.au=Ross%2C+Greg&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.americanscientist.org%2Fbookshelf%2Fpub%2Fdouglas-r-hofstadter&amp;rft.jtitle=American+Scientist&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-103">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-103">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Lyons, Daniel (May 2009).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.newsweek.com/id/197812" rel="nofollow">
           "I, Robot"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Newsweek
          </i>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2009-07-24
           </span>
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           Still, a lot of people think Kurzweil is completely bonkers and/or full of a certain messy byproduct of ordinary biological functions. They include P. Z. Myers, a biologist at the University of Minnesota, Morris, who has used his blog to poke fun at Kurzweil and other armchair futurists who, according to Myers, rely on junk science and don't understand basic biology. "I am completely baffled by Kurzweil's popularity, and in particular the respect he gets in some circles, since his claims simply do not hold up to even casually critical examination," writes Myers. He says Kurzweil's Singularity theories are closer to a deluded religious movement than they are to science. "It's a New Age spiritualismthat's all it is," Myers says. "Even geeks want to find God somewhere, and Kurzweil provides it for them."
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARay+Kurzweil&amp;rft.atitle=I%2C+Robot&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel&amp;rft.aulast=Lyons&amp;rft.au=Lyons%2C+Daniel&amp;rft.date=May+2009&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.newsweek.com%2Fid%2F197812&amp;rft.jtitle=Newsweek&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
